    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

  <span id="freeText4298776538371896697" style="display:none"><b><i>Alcatraz Versus the Evil Librarians</i> is the first adventure in a fantasy series for young readers by the #1 New York Times bestselling author Brandon Sanderson. The fast-paced and funny series is now available in deluxe hardcover editions illustrated by Hayley Lazo.</b><br /><br />On his thirteenth birthday, foster child Alcatraz Smedry gets a bag of sand in the mail-his only inheritance from his father and mother. He soon learns that this is no ordinary bag of sand. It is quickly stolen by the cult of evil Librarians who are taking over the world by spreading misinformation and suppressing truth. Alcatraz must stop them, using the only weapon he has: an incredible talent for breaking things.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This entire series is mainly about questioning author/reader conventions in the format of a children's book. It's underrated, as far as I'm concerned,<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This entire series is mainly about questioning author/reader conventions in the format of a children's book. It's underrated, as far as I'm concerned, but understandably it isn't for everyone. Essentially, just give it a go. It's mostly harmless, and it has my recommendation.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/94090129-silver---have-a-great-day-you-re-loved"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1594867307i/94090129._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/94090129-silver---have-a-great-day-you-re-loved">Silver  - Have a great day, you&#39;re loved</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This book is about a boy names Alcatraz Smedry who breaks almost anything he touches. He's a foster child who's never known his parents, and all he ge<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This book is about a boy names Alcatraz Smedry who breaks almost anything he touches. He's a foster child who's never known his parents, and all he gets from them is his name and a bag of sand on his 13th birthday. This bag of sand leads to talking dinosaurs, a fighting friend with a deadly handbag, a crazy grandpa, and evil librarians who want to rule the world. It sounds ridiculous, and it is, and that's why it's such a great book! I can't ever stop laughing when I read it.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1165302082" />
    <a title="Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/922495-patrick"><img alt="Patrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351307095p2/922495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1165302082?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/922495-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/922495-patrick?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1165302082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13219931151755756649">For the record: listened to this one on audio.<br/><br/>This book is what you'd expect from Sanderson. Good story. Nice rapid plot. An interesting well-orchestrated cosmology. And a cool magic system that's central to the story. <br/><br/>Two things of special note: <br/><br/>1. Unlike most of Sanderson's other work, this book is aimed at a YA audience. I still enjoyed it. But if you're looking for a grim, 800-page tome, this isn't it. <br/><br/>2. This book is fairly meta, especially for YA. It's first person, but the narrator regula</span>
  <span id="freeText13219931151755756649" style="display:none">For the record: listened to this one on audio.<br /><br />This book is what you'd expect from Sanderson. Good story. Nice rapid plot. An interesting well-orchestrated cosmology. And a cool magic system that's central to the story. <br /><br />Two things of special note: <br /><br />1. Unlike most of Sanderson's other work, this book is aimed at a YA audience. I still enjoyed it. But if you're looking for a grim, 800-page tome, this isn't it. <br /><br />2. This book is fairly meta, especially for YA. It's first person, but the narrator regularly intrudes and talks about what he's doing in the writing of the book. Why he's writing what he's writing. The narrative conventions he's using. <br /><br />It's an interesting addition to a story, and certainly nothing I ever ran into when I was reading as a kid.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1750351775" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1750351775" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1750351775?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780439925525" href="/book/show/3537527-alcatraz-versus-the-evil-librarians">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Artemis Fowl, Lemony Snicket</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=urban-fantasy-ya">urban-fantasy-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=fast-and-fun">fast-and-fun</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1750351775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8234056069424783448">Also known as The Official Author's Notes for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7235533.The_Way_of_Kings__The_Stormlight_Archive___1_' title='The Way of Kings (The Stormlight Archive, #1) by Brandon Sanderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Way of Kings</a>.<br/><br/>Stay with me.<br/><br/>The first clue is in Chapter 2. <b>"I've been many things in my life. Student. Spy. Sacrifice. Potted plant. However, at this point, I'm something completely different from all of those--something more frightening than any of them. I'm a writer."</b><br/><br/>He gives structural tips (and a hint as to his personality):<b><br/>"You may have noticed that I began my story with a quick, snappy scene of danger and tension--but then quickly moved on t</b></span>
  <span id="freeText8234056069424783448" style="display:none">Also known as The Official Author's Notes for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7235533.The_Way_of_Kings__The_Stormlight_Archive___1_" title="The Way of Kings (The Stormlight Archive, #1) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Way of Kings</a>.<br /><br />Stay with me.<br /><br />The first clue is in Chapter 2. <b>"I've been many things in my life. Student. Spy. Sacrifice. Potted plant. However, at this point, I'm something completely different from all of those--something more frightening than any of them. I'm a writer."</b><br /><br />He gives structural tips (and a hint as to his personality):<b><br />"You may have noticed that I began my story with a quick, snappy scene of danger and tension--but then quickly moved on to a more boring discussion of my childhood. Well, that's because I wanted to prove something to you: that <i>I'm not a nice person."</i></b><br /><br />He boldly states how he would like you to read:<b> <br />"I would ask you to kindly refrain from drawing conclusions that I don't explicitly tell you to make. That's a very bad habit, and it makes authors grumpy."</b><br /><br />Unsurprisingly, he trumpets the importance of his work:<b><br />"Remember, despite the fact that this book is being sold as a 'fantasy' novel, you must take all of the things it says extremely seriously, as they are quite important, are in no way silly, and always make sense."</b><br /><br />He explains his plot devices to engage the reader:<b><br />"I've worked very hard--perhaps I will explain why later--to frustrate you. One of the ways I do this is by leaving cliff hangers at the ends of chapters. These sorts of things force you, the reader, to keep on plunging through my story." </b>He does this despite further elaboration that a hook at the beginning of a book is an 'unexcusable' trick, and that<b> "I have it on good authority that when an author gives a hook like this, he isn't ever likely to explain why...and, if the explanation does come, it won't arrive until the end of the story."</b><br /><br />Ultimately, he expresses his writing goal, which should have been quite obvious if you follow the <i>Way of Kings</i> ten book series, now up to book two:<b> "Authors write books for one, and only one reason: because we like to torture people." </b>He continues: <b>"Authors also create lovable, friendly characters--then proceed to do terrible things to them... This makes readers feel hurt and worried for the characters. The simple truth is that authors <i>like</i> making people squirm."</b><br /><br />Given my concerns with <i>Way of Kings,</i> I appreciated his notes regarding time in novels: <b>"Three chapters is an awfully long time in book terms. You see, time moves differently in novels. The author could, for instance, say, "And I spent fourteen years in prison...." Now this sounds like it would be a great deal of time--fourteen <i>years</i>--but it actually only took one sentence to explain. So, therefore, it happened very quickly. Three chapters, on the other hand, is a very long time."</b><br /><br />And a final bon mot on pacing:<br /><b>"Now, if you are ever writing a story such as this, you should know something. Never interrupt the flow of a good action scene by interjecting needless explanations. I did this once, in Chapter Fourteen of an otherwise very exciting story. I regret it to this day."</b><br /><br />I tell you, I gained tremendous insight into <i>The Way of Kings.</i><br /><br />But I know what you are going to say:<br /><br />I read it wrong.<br /><br />My review for <i>Way of Kings</i>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/169319377">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br />P.S. I really enjoyed the polite dinosaurs.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />So, a real review, you ask? Why are you asking me? You should read Sanderson yourself, because I'm quite sure I'm going to mislead you by reading it wrong. I enjoy many younger-adult targeted books, so don't think me an old curmudgeon when I say he doesn't quite nail the premise. It is vaguely amusing when he mocks many of the genre pretenses (particularly a bold call-out to the Harry Potter set-up at the end), but there's too much of it throughout the narrative and I'm not sure it'll sit well with younger readers. Really much, much too much of the overt commentary. When I started writing my meta-review (thanks, Mitticus!), I actually had to leave out some more author in-text comments on character and pacing. John Connolly's Samuel Johnson series plays with this concept in a more sophisticated, enjoyable way way.<br /><br />In this book, Alcatraz is about to be kicked out of his umpteenth foster home for burning down the kitchen on his 13th birthday. Someone calling himself his grandfather shows up the next day (much like Hagrid in Harry Potter) and suddenly someone is trying to kill him. Classic special-but-in-an-unrecognized-way set-up. They head to the library to infiltrate the headquarters and recover Alcatraz' special birthday present--a bag of sand. Fun things include the premise of Librarians being Evil, and running jokes about the gentility of dinosaurs. However, Alcatraz also has a anti-hero narrative in the mode of Artemis Fowl that is off-putting. It's too much tongue-in-cheek; what, exactly, are we supposed to take seriously here? The finale was disappointing, particularly with another big reveal for Alcatraz (really, when is enough enough)? <br /><br />Overall, I'd say it was middle-of the road. I'll throw out the idea that Sanderson just is... odd about female characters. Like he's trying too hard and just ends up doing reverse stereotypes.The Evil Librarians are the best concept behind it, and the humorous tone is cute. Aside from that, it lacks the inventiveness of Potter and the Girl Who... series, the language playfulness of Valente and Snicket, the commitment to devilishness of Artemis and the cleverness of Connolly. Most importantly, I just don't feel the emotional truth it needs. Would I pick up the next book? Sure. Would I give it to a future niece? Nah. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="8234056069424783448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_762271075" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/762271075" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/762271075?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer762271075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10825444123191371332">Meet MC; his name is Al short for Alcatraz (it is not his fault the evil librarians use the most famous names of his dynasty for the most notorious prisons). The book starts with poor guy being tied to a bunch of outdated encyclopedias and is about to be sacrificed (Indiana Jones and the Tempe of Doom way) – say what you want about the evil librarians, but they sure got style.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470934247i/19982974.jpg' width='400' height='300' alt='Temple of Doom' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/> <br/>Chronologically it all started innocently enough. Alcatraz was an orphan who was changing foster parents faster than yo</span>
  <span id="freeText10825444123191371332" style="display:none">Meet MC; his name is Al short for Alcatraz (it is not his fault the evil librarians use the most famous names of his dynasty for the most notorious prisons). The book starts with poor guy being tied to a bunch of outdated encyclopedias and is about to be sacrificed (Indiana Jones and the Tempe of Doom way) – say what you want about the evil librarians, but they sure got style.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470934247i/19982974.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="Temple of Doom" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br> <br>Chronologically it all started innocently enough. Alcatraz was an orphan who was changing foster parents faster than you can say, “supercalifragilisticexpialidocious”. He had no clue about his parents or any living relatives until he received a gift for his thirteenth birthday, supposedly from his father. Inside the package there was a bunch of sand and nothing else. It seemed like a pointless poor joke except for the fact that the said sand caused Alcatraz to meet a crazy guy claiming to be his grandfather and to follow him down the rabbit hole – literally speaking.<br> <br>You see, the world as we know it is controlled by evil librarians through careful distribution and suppression of information. They are about to conquer what remained outside of their influence and Alcatraz had the key to opposing them. Whether he wanted or not, he was in the game: a gun pointed at you from a blank point range makes you decide which side you are on really fast.<br> <br>If all of the about sounds like a cliché, you are completely right. Brandon Sanderson makes fun of a lot of them among other things. Do not take this book seriously as it is not supposed to and you will like it.<br> <br>Brandon Sanderson has a lot of dedicated fans. For this reason I am very surprised at the relative obscurity of this series which I would not hesitate to call quite underrated. I forgot the last time I read equally good humorous YA fantasy. I also learned that Sanderson can write funny humorous books – a lot of people can write humorous books, but funny is something only few succeed in. When the book is not funny it is at least amusing.<br> <br>One example of this: there is a guy who has a very powerful talent: he is always late. How powerful the talent it? It turned out the guy is impossible to kill with a gun as he would be late for the meeting with his bullet. Another guy has a talent for very effective falling down. Once again it turns out he does it right before a real danger so if you see him doing this you better follow his example and hope you hit the floor faster than him.<br> <br>My only complaint about the book is the following. The narrator – Alcatraz himself – often breaks the fourth wall. While it is always amusing, for me it comes out way over the top and sometimes forced to be really funny. This is even though one such breakage contains possibly the best part of the book: I am talking about Alcatraz’s musing about sadistic authors – spot on. This in my only complaint, but it is a big one.<br> <br>To make a long story short the rating is firm 4 stars and I will most definitely continue reading the series. Avoid it like plague if you are in the mood for something serious like a book about a dying dog, or something similar (I am quoting Alcatraz here), otherwise read it and have a good laugh. All hail evil librarians!!!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470934284i/19982982.jpg" width="460" height="348" alt="Evil Librarians" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="10825444123191371332" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1593245274" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1593245274" />
    <a title="Twila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4585336-twila"><img alt="Twila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585941160p2/4585336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1593245274?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Twila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Twila" href="/user/show/4585336-twila">Twila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765378941" href="/book/show/25403108-alcatraz-vs-the-evil-librarians">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Rick Riordan and Eoin Colfer</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4585336-twila?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4585336-twila?shelf=could-not-put-down">could-not-put-down</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4585336-twila?shelf=cute">cute</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4585336-twila?shelf=made-me-laugh">made-me-laugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4585336-twila?shelf=what-did-i-just-read">what-did-i-just-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4585336-twila?shelf=favourite-authors">favourite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4585336-twila?shelf=made-me-think">made-me-think</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4585336-twila?shelf=timey-wimey">timey-wimey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4585336-twila?shelf=unforgettable">unforgettable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4585336-twila?shelf=fantastic-narration">fantastic-narration</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1593245274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9248021435829779617">5 EYE-OPENING ST★RS<br/><br/><b>Heads up! Goodreads librarian agents might try to get this review taken down at any moment! They definitely don’t want me exposing all their secretly nefarious ways, but at long last, I give to you the truth:</b><br/><br/><u>Fact #1:</u> This book is NOT written by Brandon Sanderson. <br/><br/>This is NOT “fantasy”. Don’t be fooled. It is written by Alcatraz Smedry—grandson of Oculator Dramatus, Leavenworth Smedry. His editor only made him use Sanderson’s name to keep away librarian attention. This is Alcat</span>
  <span id="freeText9248021435829779617" style="display:none">5 EYE-OPENING ST★RS<br /><br /><b>Heads up! Goodreads librarian agents might try to get this review taken down at any moment! They definitely don’t want me exposing all their secretly nefarious ways, but at long last, I give to you the truth:</b><br /><br /><u>Fact #1:</u> This book is NOT written by Brandon Sanderson. <br /><br />This is NOT “fantasy”. Don’t be fooled. It is written by Alcatraz Smedry—grandson of Oculator Dramatus, Leavenworth Smedry. His editor only made him use Sanderson’s name to keep away librarian attention. This is Alcatraz’s autobiography, okay?! Nonfiction! <br /><br /><u>Fact #2:</u> Librarians are evil. <br /><br />I should have known. They always made me feel uncomfortable with all their <i>staring</i> and constant hovering while in libraries. Now I know the reason for their insistent vigilance. They are making sure this book and others like it stay out of public hands! That's pretty much how they rule the world. They control all the information and supposed “knowledge” given to us—info that we sadly just accept. But I’m not being restricted from the truth any longer. They kept this book a secret from me for years, but now that I have it, I’m holding it tight.<br /><br /><u>Fact #3:</u> The Smedrys are civilization’s only hope! <br /><br />They’ve been trying to save us from total domination by using their special powers called “Talents”. Talents can range from anything like being terrible at math to waking up extremely ugly to tripping in fantastically glorious ways. Alcatraz has the breaking Talent. HE CAN BREAK THINGS WITH THE FORCE OF HIS MIND. How epic! And he’s about to face his toughest challenge yet, infiltrating his downtown library—an <i>extremely</i> dangerous place—to retrieve a lost bag of sand and save the world. Oh yeah. <br /><br /><u>So there you have it. The <b>truth.</b></u> Strange, right? Brilliantly strange. And weird. But not only is Alcatraz’s story incredibly funny and jam-packed with action, it’s filled with heart as well. Underneath all the fun humour and cringeworthy puns, this is story that surprisingly carries across subtle messages about responsibility and courage, trust and self-confidence—all while you’ll be laughing out loud.<br /><br />It actually felt somewhat meaningful, but anyway, back to the important stuff. The Librarians want to control the entire world. We can’t let them. Will you join me in the fight to stop their evil cult? <br /><br /><b>Go read it and help me spread the word! GO! GO!</b><br /><br /><br />P.S. To all my librarian friends: Please don't hate me for exposing you. I know you're evil and all, but I love you guys.</span>

<div id="review_1131402062" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1131402062" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1131402062?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25753608-alcatraz-vs-the-evil-librarians">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=brandon-sanderson">brandon-sanderson</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=dr-reading-challenge">dr-reading-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1131402062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6239241021069632860">Brandon Sanderson can write an instruction manual for a lawnmower and I’ll read it. <i>(I actually have no reason at all to know how to use a lawnmower since I live in a high-rise condominium).</i> <br/><br/>I only started reading the Alcatraz series after I’ve run out of Sanderson's adult and YA fantasy books to read, and <b>these books quickly became bite-sized guilty pleasures on account of how hilarious and ridiculous they are.</b> <br/><br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>In the Hushlands—those Librarian-controlled nations such as the United State</blockquote></b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText6239241021069632860" style="display:none">Brandon Sanderson can write an instruction manual for a lawnmower and I’ll read it. <i>(I actually have no reason at all to know how to use a lawnmower since I live in a high-rise condominium).</i> <br><br>I only started reading the Alcatraz series after I’ve run out of Sanderson's adult and YA fantasy books to read, and <b>these books quickly became bite-sized guilty pleasures on account of how hilarious and ridiculous they are.</b> <br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>In the Hushlands—those Librarian-controlled nations such as the United States, Canada, and England—this book will be published as a work of fantasy. Do not be fooled! This is no work of fiction, nor is my name really Brandon Sanderson. Both are guises to hide the book from Librarian agents. Unfortunately, even with these precautions, I suspect that the Librarians will discover the book and ban it. In that case, our Free Kingdom Agents will have to sneak into libraries and bookstores to put it on shelves. Count yourself lucky if you’ve found one of these secret copies.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>So essentially, the real world as we know it is controlled by evil Librarians who keep the real deal/information away from the general population. Underneath the cover-up is a more fantastical existence where a certain lineage of people (i.e. the Smedry's) have seemingly ordinary 'abilities' like breaking things, being late, spouting gibberish and tripping; abilities which are called Talents that can be controlled and utilised as an advantage. How this works is frankly quite brilliant and instead of explaining it, let me point you to the nearest bookstore (online or otherwise) to get hold of this book and read it already. <br><br><b>The map of world as we (did not) know it</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1501077817i/23414869._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am pretty sure that I don’t have to mention that Sanderson has yet again conjured a cool magic system for this series, and demonstrated the magic in his usual well-crafted action scenes. In this series, it involves sand and ocular lenses. How? Just read it and find out! <br><br>The main character, Alcatraz Smedry is written in a first person, fourth-wall breaking perspective. His POV is sarcastic, witty and gives the impression that he can be an unreliable narrator. Each chapter also begins with asides and jabs regarding books and authors, all which ring true.<br><br>A few examples:<br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>It is a writer’s greatest pleasure to hear that someone was kept up until the unholy hours of the morning reading one of his books. Plus we get a kickback from the caffeine industry.<br>------------------------<br>Hooks and cliffhangers belong only at the ends of chapters. That way, the reader moves on directly to the next page—where, thankfully, they can read more of the story without having to suffer some sort of mindless interruption. Honestly, authors can be so self-indulgent.<br>------------------------<br>The ending of a book is, in my experience, both the best and the worst part to read. For the ending will often determine whether you love or hate the book. Both emotions lead to disappointment. If the ending was good, and the book was worth your time, then you are left annoyed and depressed because there is no more book to read. However, if the ending was bad, then it’s too late to stop reading. You’re left annoyed and depressed because you wasted so much time on a book with a bad ending.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>What else is there? There are references to Sanderson’s own works and of other authors’ peppered throughout the story, which add to the fun factor. This new edition also has great illustrations that truly enhance the enjoyment of the book. The typical back matter, "About The Author" and "Acknowledgements", is anything but typical. <br><br><b>Here's Grandpa!</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1501077817i/23414868._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is a book and series targeted for the young readers as well as adults who want to kick back with some silly, yet quite smart, humour. Character development was adequate in spite of the shorter narrative and I already have a favourite in Grandpa Smedry by the end of this novel. The writing is relatively simple but not condescendingly so in spite of the target middle grade audience. Given that it is a lot shorter than your typical Sanderson doorstopper, the pacing was brisk and action scenes were plenty and fun. It's like a light and fruity dessert after a heavy meal.<br><br><i>This review can also be found at <a href="http://booknest.eu/review/ts-reviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Booknest</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6239241021069632860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1729527680" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1729527680" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1729527680?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=brandon-sanderson">brandon-sanderson</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=childrens-books">childrens-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=advanture">advanture</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1729527680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12138631303446070880">*** 4 ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with the young at heart folks at BBB! <br/><br/>This sucks!!! I had written a review, I had made it funny and adorable, as well as recommended this book not only to the middle graders for whom it was written, but also to all those who enjoy a fantastical adventure written with such wonderful flare and wit, that you have no choice but fall in love with it and wonder why the heck did you wait so long to get to this brilliant series!!!! I had written it, but somehow it has gotten lost i</span>
  <span id="freeText12138631303446070880" style="display:none">*** 4 ***<br /><br />A buddy read with the young at heart folks at BBB! <br /><br />This sucks!!! I had written a review, I had made it funny and adorable, as well as recommended this book not only to the middle graders for whom it was written, but also to all those who enjoy a fantastical adventure written with such wonderful flare and wit, that you have no choice but fall in love with it and wonder why the heck did you wait so long to get to this brilliant series!!!! I had written it, but somehow it has gotten lost in the twilight zone of GR....<br /><br />I am not planning to try and write another marvelous review, since I only write them at the moment when I complete the read, thus infusing them with my emotions at the moment... However, I will tell you that the book's protagonist is the 13 year old Alcatraz Smedry, a boy with a very special talent - he can break almost everything he comes in contact with, usually without even wanting to... He is also a writer. <br /><br />...It is a writer's greatest pleasure to hear that someone was kept up until the unholy hours of the morning reading one of his books. It goes back to authors being terrible people who delight in the suffering of others. Plus, we get a kickback from the caffeine industry...” <br /><br />...“Authors also create lovable, friendly characters, then proceed to do terrible things to them, like throw them in unsightly librarian-controlled dungeons. This makes readers feel hurt and worried for the characters. The simple truth is that authors like making people squirm. If this weren't the case, all novels would be filled completely with cute bunnies having birthday parties.”...<br /><br />Hey, those are his words, not mine.... <br /><br />So, the world we live in, apparently, is not at all what we think. What we think we know about our world has been force-fed to us by the most evil of Evil Cults - The Cult of the Evil Librarians!!! After all, what better way to feed us faulty knowledge than take over the Libraries and all educational facilities and books, thus making us believe whatever They want... ? Exactly!!! <br /><br /><br />...“So, there I was, tied to an altar made from outdated encyclopedias, about to get sacrificed to the dark powers by a cult of evil Librarians.”...<br /><br /><br />Hmmm, I am going too deep... Needles to say, the books we read are mostly lies, thus evil, and Alcatraz is here to open our eyes to the truth!!! So, instead of me telling you how important it is for you to read this series, let me finish with Alcatraz's own words:<br /><br />.... Actually, my experience has been that people generally don’t recommend this kind of book at all. It is far too interesting. Perhaps you have had other kinds of books recommended to you. Perhaps, even, you have been given books by friends, parents, or teachers, then told that these books are the type you “have to read.” Those books are invariably described as “important” – which, in my experience, pretty much means that they’re boring. (Words like meaningful and thoughtful are other good clues.) If there is a boy in these kinds of books, he will not go on an adventure to fight against Librarians, paper monsters, and one-eyed Dark Oculators.<br /><br />In fact, the lad will not go on an adventure or fight against anything at all. Instead, his dog will die. Or, in some cases, his mother will die. If it’s a really meaningful book, both his dog and his mother will die. (Apparently, most writers have something against dogs and mothers.)”... <br /><br />I wish all of you Happy reading and don't get caught by the Evil Librarians!!!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1696378387?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">EVERYONE...fans of Rick Riordan and J.K. Rowling</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=uf-pnr">uf-pnr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1696378387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18118406359787783404">On sale Sept 7 2016 on <a href='https://www.amazon.com/Alcatraz-vs-Evil-Librarians-Versus-ebook/dp/B00XHHV2A0/ref=as_li_ss_il?ie=UTF8&psc=1&refRID=FN6CBR0E1JPF1078B500&linkCode=li1&tag=rabrea-20&linkId=693f0032c3381ca390778856e5743331#nav-subnav' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> for $2.99<br/><br/>Buddy Read with <b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books and Baubles</a> and the Sandersonitus gang.</b><br/><br/><b>Did you know that Librarians were evil???</b> I’ve always suspected but didn’t know just how deep the conspiracy went until I read this book.<br/><br/>What does a writer do when he needs to get the creative juices going and take a break from one of the many serious tombs he is writing? <b> Well if he is Brandon Sanderson he writes something completely and utterly different and a bit silly and makes fun of </b></span>
  <span id="freeText18118406359787783404" style="display:none">On sale Sept 7 2016 on <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Alcatraz-vs-Evil-Librarians-Versus-ebook/dp/B00XHHV2A0/ref=as_li_ss_il?ie=UTF8&amp;psc=1&amp;refRID=FN6CBR0E1JPF1078B500&amp;linkCode=li1&amp;tag=rabrea-20&amp;linkId=693f0032c3381ca390778856e5743331#nav-subnav" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> for $2.99<br><br>Buddy Read with <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a> and the Sandersonitus gang.</b><br><br><b>Did you know that Librarians were evil???</b> I’ve always suspected but didn’t know just how deep the conspiracy went until I read this book.<br><br>What does a writer do when he needs to get the creative juices going and take a break from one of the many serious tombs he is writing? <b> Well if he is Brandon Sanderson he writes something completely and utterly different and a bit silly and makes fun of himself a little while doing it.</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>Now, you’re probably wondering about the beginning of the previous chapter, with its reference to evil Librarians, altars made from encyclopedias, and its general feeling of “Oh, no! Alcatraz is going to be sacrificed!” Before we get to this, let me explain something about myself.<b> I’ve been many things in my life. Student. Spy. Sacrifice. Potted plant.</b> However, at this point, I’m something completely different from all of those—something more frightening than any of them. <br>I’m a writer.</i>
</blockquote><br>As an adult in my *cough*fouthir*cough*ties Middle Grade books aren’t my bread and butter. I actually rarely read them. HOWEVER….there are a few writers that can make a middle grade book just as fun for the adults as the kids…sorta like Bugs Bunny. Sanderson to my surprise <i>(I’m not really sure why I was that surprised I love most of his stuff)</i> now joins that very short list with Rick Riordan and J.K. Rowling as one of my favorite Middle Grade Authors.<br><br>This book is hi-LAR-i-OUS all the way though from beginning to end. There are so many funny instances and things happening throughout the story I laughed continuously. There is the continuous breaking of the 4th wall and side jaunts as our young Alcatraz talks to the reader. I loved almost all of them and the story was totally engaging for me all the way through.<br><blockquote>
  <i>I generally don’t recommend this kind of book at all. It is far too interesting. Perhaps you have had other kinds of books recommended to you. Perhaps, even, you have been given books by friends, parents, or teachers, then told that these books are the type you “have to read.” Those books are invariably described as “important”—which, in my experience, pretty much means that they’re boring. (Words like meaningful and thoughtful are other good clues.) If there is a boy in these kinds of books, he will not go on an adventure to fight against Librarians, paper monsters, and one-eyed Dark Oculators.<b> In fact, the lad will not go on an adventure or fight against anything at all. Instead, his dog will die. Or, in some cases, his mother will die. If it’s a really meaningful book, both his dog and his mother will die.</b> (Apparently, most writers have something against dogs and mothers.) </i>
</blockquote><br><b>The Rundown:</b><br><br>Alcatraz is an orphaned boy who just turned 13 and realized that he has special powers and is needed to SAVE THE WORLD….sound familiar??? Well it is but he can’t fly or turn invisible, he doesn’t have super strength or the ability to transport himself across distances. No his special power is…..<b>he can break things</b>…tah dahhhhh. Your thinking that hey I too can break things and that doesn’t sound like it is all that special. Well you are wrong and you are probably a librarian or a hushlander who doesn’t understand the awesomeness of breaking things.<br><i>“What kinds of things can you break?” Grandpa Smedry asked.<br>“All kinds of things,” I said. “Doors, electronics, tables. Once I broke a chicken.”<br>“A chicken?”<br>I nodded. “It was on a field trip. I got … kind of frustrated, and I picked up a chicken. When I put it down, it immediately lost all of its feathers, and from then on refused to eat anything but cat food.”</i><br>Alcatraz isn’t the only one who has a superpower. No indeed everyone in the main line of his family can do something special. Like his Cousin Sing who can trip, a Grandfather who can be late and another cousin that…..<br><blockquote><i>“And what is your Talent?” I dutifully asked. <br>“I can say things that make absolutely no sense whatsoever.” <br>“I thought everyone here had that Talent,” I noted. Nobody laughed. Free Kingdomers never get my jokes.</i></blockquote><br>Don’t worry Alcatraz I got all your jokes and they were hilarious.<br><br>So as superpowers go they sound a little lame….but trust me, when you see how they work you will be AMAZED and ENTERTAINED. There are also knights, <b>monsters made out of bad romance novels</b> and glasses that you will be dying to get a pair of. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471643333i/20085856._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="207" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you have read a Sanderson novel then you know that the world building and magic system is going to be great. It will be imaginative and inventive and there will be a twist. Even though this is a kid’s book….it is so not just a kid’s book. There is a little something for everyone and I can’t believe I waited so long to read these.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470109257i/19888432._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="418" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I bow down again to the writing Genius that is Sanderson and can’t wait to jump into the next book of the series.</b> Fun for all ages.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="18118406359787783404" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1156084339?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1156084339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15218478678085811793"><div>
  <p>Think Harry Potter only with evil Librarians but a lot better.</p>
  <p>Although it’s obviously written for young readers, it was still entertaining for adults. The story was fast paced and very humorous. The characters are fun and relatable as far possible in this type of story. It’s a quick read and well worth it.</p>
  <p> Perfect for kids. I think it would be a great bedtime story that parents could read with their kids. If anyone still does that.</p>
</div></span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="J.L.   Sutton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3675162-j-l-sutton"><img alt="J.L.   Sutton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438142892p2/3675162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.L.   Sutton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.L.   Sutton" href="/user/show/3675162-j-l-sutton">J.L.   Sutton</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2232362930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13159948701860100826">Big fan of Brandon Sanderson. It's always interesting to think about the magic system Sanderson uses in whatever work you're reading. He always changes things up. Alcatraz Versus the Evil Librarians is no exception. In this fun read, Alcatraz's talent is his uncanny ability to break things. While this might not seem like part of a magical system at first, keep reading! I enjoyed the book and plan to get back to this series. But maybe after I read Oathbringer! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1543055497" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1543055497" />
    <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc"><img alt="Mogsy (MMOGC)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286325553p2/4379514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1543055497?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mogsy (MMOGC)" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc">Mogsy (MMOGC)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765378941" href="/book/show/25403108-alcatraz-vs-the-evil-librarians">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1543055497" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3189851640248397300">5 of 5 stars at the BiblioSanctum <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://bibliosanctum.com/2016/02/22/series-review-alcatraz-vs-the-evil-librarians-books-1-2-by-brandon-sanderson/'>http://bibliosanctum.com/2016/02/22/s...</a><br/><br/>I’ve been a terrible Brandon Sanderson fan! Seriously, how else to explain for the many years it took me to finally read his Alcatraz series? Mea culpa, it was complete negligence on my part, and I am sorry. But in my own defense, these books do fall a little outside my purview. After all, very rarely do I dip my toes into the Children’s/Middle Grade category, and they did seem far removed from the author’s other work. By </span>
  <span id="freeText3189851640248397300" style="display:none">5 of 5 stars at the BiblioSanctum <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bibliosanctum.com/2016/02/22/series-review-alcatraz-vs-the-evil-librarians-books-1-2-by-brandon-sanderson/">http://bibliosanctum.com/2016/02/22/s...</a><br /><br />I’ve been a terrible Brandon Sanderson fan! Seriously, how else to explain for the many years it took me to finally read his Alcatraz series? Mea culpa, it was complete negligence on my part, and I am sorry. But in my own defense, these books do fall a little outside my purview. After all, very rarely do I dip my toes into the Children’s/Middle Grade category, and they did seem far removed from the author’s other work. By his own admission, this series is very different from his normal style and they tend to be a source of contention among his readers. Don’t let that stop you if you think this might be something you’ll enjoy, though! Personally, I jumped into this first book amidst a bevy of reservations, but I ended up loving it to bits.<br /><br />Alcatraz vs. The Evil Librarians is the first in a fantasy adventure series featuring its eponymous protagonist who is narrating this book as its writer—“Brandon Sanderson” is just a front, you see. The real person behind this novel is a young boy named Alcatraz Smedry. He is thirteen years old and lives with his foster parents. He is also great at breaking things. It all began with an old bag of sand, mailed to Alcatraz on his birthday—the only inheritance left to him by his birth parents. But before you can even say “Gee, thanks mom and dad”, the bag is stolen by a member of the Librarians, an evil cult that knows the sand is more than it seems. For centuries, they have been controlling information and spreading lies to keep everyone blind to their dastardly plans of world domination, but now that Alcatraz has learned the truth of his birthright, he and his new allies are going to strike back at the heart of the enemy—by planning a daring mission to infiltrate the central downtown library.<br /><br />Don’t let the synopsis of the book fool you, because the utter absurdity of the plot actually belies its sheer ingenuity. The story is clever and beyond hilarious, thanks to the playfully sarcastic voice of our protagonist. Alcatraz himself is a bit of a trickster, often going on wildly bizarre tangents and freely admitting that he’s not a very nice person for yanking the reader around. Still, I could hardly hold that against him, considering the many times his narration drove me to hysterical fits of laughter. This is Sanderson at his funniest, combining his good-natured humor with a spirit of adventure. More than once I found myself wishing there had been books like this when I was a child, because I would have eaten this one up.<br /><br />That said, just because these are “kids’ books” doesn’t mean adults can’t enjoy them too. My favorite stories are always those that can be appreciated an audience of all ages, and Alcatraz vs. The Evil Librarians definitely fits that description, being a book I would readily recommend to anyone, whether they are 13 or 30. While it does feature some over-the-top storytelling, never once did I feel things were dumbed down or glossed over unnecessarily. In fact, the plot was decidedly twisty and unpredictable, with some very well thought out and complex ideas. From the very first page you get a sense of the zaniness behind this novel and the anticipatory feeling that anything can happen.<br /><br />For a personal project that began life as a way for the author to have a good time and practice another form of storytelling, this book has certainly found itself a loyal fanbase, which I now consider myself a part of. Alcatraz may be very different from Sanderon’s adult books, but it nevertheless shows his incredible versatility as a writer, and you can tell he had a blast writing this. Clearly, I had a blast reading it too, and the gorgeous artwork by Hayley Lazo in the illustrated edition only added to the experience. I can’t wait to read the rest of the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3189851640248397300" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1550765894" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1550765894" />
    <a title="Bookwraiths" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths"><img alt="Bookwraiths" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353765210p2/14716035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1550765894?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookwraiths" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookwraiths" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths">Bookwraiths</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765378941" href="/book/show/25403108-alcatraz-vs-the-evil-librarians">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=young_adult">young_adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=review-freebie">review-freebie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=middle-grades">middle-grades</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1550765894" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2944045138489800718">Originally reviewed at <a href='http://bookwraiths.com/2016/03/26/alcatraz-versus-the-evil-librarians/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bookwraiths</a> <br/><br/>The first adventure in the young adult fantasy series <i>Alcatraz The Evil Librarians</i> was one which I and my youngest son read as a bedtime story. As a fan of Rick Riordan’s <i>Percy Jackson</i> series and Mac Barnett’s <i>Brixton Brothers</i> mysteries, I knew the novel was a can’t miss with the little Bookwraith, and I wasn’t wrong. This fast-paced, funny tale by Brandon Sanderson bringing more than a few smiles to my face and eliciting many a hysterical giggle from my son, w</span>
  <span id="freeText2944045138489800718" style="display:none">Originally reviewed at <a href="http://bookwraiths.com/2016/03/26/alcatraz-versus-the-evil-librarians/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookwraiths</a> <br /><br />The first adventure in the young adult fantasy series <i>Alcatraz The Evil Librarians</i> was one which I and my youngest son read as a bedtime story. As a fan of Rick Riordan’s <i>Percy Jackson</i> series and Mac Barnett’s <i>Brixton Brothers</i> mysteries, I knew the novel was a can’t miss with the little Bookwraith, and I wasn’t wrong. This fast-paced, funny tale by Brandon Sanderson bringing more than a few smiles to my face and eliciting many a hysterical giggle from my son, which meant it was great fun but didn’t really put him to sleep any faster.<br /><br />In this story, foster child Alcatraz Smedry is our star. Like most thirteen year olds, he has more than a little teen angst going on, but Alcatraz has more than a little right to feel that way, because he has had a pretty rough life: losing his parents, moving from foster home to foster home, and being cursed with a knack to break almost anything. And when he gets a bag of sand in the mail for his birthday, his angst only grows, as it seems this is his only inheritance from his mom and dad.<br /><br />Soon, though, Alcatraz learns that there is a lot more to this stupid bag of sand than he thought. A cult of evil Librarians (who plan on taking over the world by distorting the truth) stealing it from him, trying to shot him before a strange, old man in a modified Model T-Ford slams his car into the side of Alcatraz’s house.<br /><br />Grandpa Smedry not only saves Alcatraz but opens his eyes to a whole new world. A place where the Free Kingdoms are waging a hidden war against the Evil Librarians, and Alcatraz’s inheritance of a bag of sand is the most powerful gift anyone could have ever been given. (It took Alcatraz’s dad his whole life to gather the Sands of Rashid one grain at a time!) The Librarians wanting the sands, because with them they will be able to create the most powerful Oculatory Distortions ever, giving them the power to finally overthrow the Free Kingdoms!<br /><br />Well, at least, Grandpa Smedry says all this is true. Alcatraz isn’t really sure if he believes him or not, especially the part about him being his grandpa. So what is he to do: run off into unknown danger with a strange man who might be delusional or head off to another foster home?<br /><br />Finally, our young orphan decides, telling Grandpa Smedry, “<i>I’m only going with you because someone just tried to kill me. You see, I’m a somewhat reckless boy and not always prone to carefully considering the consequences of my actions.</i>”<br /><br />But how will the odd pair retrieve the sands from the armed and dangerous Librarians?<br /><br />Grandpa Smedry has the answer: They will use Alcatraz’s Smedry talent. The talent (not a curse at all) to break things. The most powerful Smedry talent ever!<br /><br />Lighthearted, funny, and filled with wild, crazy ideas sure to delight everyone who has the heart of a child, <i>Alcatraz versus the Evil Librarians</i> shows a very different side of Brandon Sanderson, but it still displays all his amazing storytelling talents: amazing plot, interesting characters, and mesmerizing twists and turns, which means it is a story not to be missed.<br /><br />I received this book from the Starscape Books in exchange for a fair and honest review. I’d like to thank the publishers for allowing me to receive this review copy and inform everyone that the review you have read is my opinion alone.<br /></span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4934375848134322396"><b>Only <s>Alcatraz</s> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson' title='Brandon Sanderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sanderson</a> can take something as mundane as sand and an orphan klutz and turn it into this amazing piece of work!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515004398i/24824173._SX540_.jpg' width='564' height='461' alt='Alcatraz' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><u>First Sentence:</u> <i>So, there I was, tied to an altar made from outdated encyclopedias, about to get sacrificed to the dark powers by a cult of evil Librarians.<i></i><br/><br/> </i><p>I really enjoyed this, the humor is spot on, the sarcasm and quips make you laugh out loud. <br/>The plot is lively, entertaining and full of twists and turns that you might - or might not have predicted. And of course one</p></span>
  <span id="freeText4934375848134322396" style="display:none"><b>Only <s>Alcatraz</s> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson" title="Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Sanderson</a> can take something as mundane as sand and an orphan klutz and turn it into this amazing piece of work!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515004398i/24824173._SX540_.jpg" width="564" height="461" alt="Alcatraz" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>First Sentence:</u> <i>So, there I was, tied to an altar made from outdated encyclopedias, about to get sacrificed to the dark powers by a cult of evil Librarians.<i></i><br><br> </i><p>I really enjoyed this, the humor is spot on, the sarcasm and quips make you laugh out loud. <br>The plot is lively, entertaining and full of twists and turns that you might - or might not have predicted. And of course one of the most unique and entrancing magical systems you'll ever read about.</p> <p>The distinctive style in which this book is written is the true joy. Told as an AUTOBIOGRAPHY, <s>Alcatraz</s> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson" title="Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Sanderson</a> takes us on his journey of how he discovered his true inheritance.<br>Forget everything you ever thought you knew, and go read this book.<br>An unfortunate hero, will tell you exactly why he isn't a hero. And you will never look at Librarians the same way.</p></span>

    <a title="Mario" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16628840-mario"><img alt="Mario" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588674821p2/16628840.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1402970082?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario" href="/user/show/16628840-mario">Mario</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444006681" href="/book/show/17245762-alcatraz-versus-the-evil-librarians">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1402970082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10792288925687555625"><i>So, when people try to give you some book with a shiny round award on the cover, be kind and gracious, but tell them you don't read "fantasy," because you prefer stories that are real. Then come back here and continue your research on the cult of evil Librarians who secretly rule the world.</i><br/><br/><br/>Will it ever come a day when I'll give Brandon Sanderson less than 5 stars? I don't think so.<br/><br/><i>Alcatraz Versus the Evil Librarians</i> was so much fun to read. I think the humor was my favorite part of this book. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText10792288925687555625" style="display:none"><i>So, when people try to give you some book with a shiny round award on the cover, be kind and gracious, but tell them you don't read "fantasy," because you prefer stories that are real. Then come back here and continue your research on the cult of evil Librarians who secretly rule the world.</i><br /><br /><br />Will it ever come a day when I'll give Brandon Sanderson less than 5 stars? I don't think so.<br /><br /><i>Alcatraz Versus the Evil Librarians</i> was so much fun to read. I think the humor was my favorite part of this book. The main character, Alcatraz, is one of the funniest character I've read about (right up there with Percy Jackson). I loved the way he narrated the story and his way of thinking. And even though he was my favorite character, I still really liked all of our other main characters (especially Bastille).<br /><br />One more thing I want to mention is the magic system. Yet again, Sanderson managed to create an amazing magic system, and though it is a little weird, it fit the story perfectly.<br /><br />I'll definitely continue on with the series, maybe not right away, but in near future. I'll be crazy not to. And if you're fan of Sanderson, or just like to read fun and exciting books, give this one a shot. I don’t think you'll be disappointed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10792288925687555625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1721492811" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1375923299696389559">5 stars for pure entertainment value. I laughed my ass off reading this book. <br/><br/>Alcatraz Versus the Evil Librarians is about Alcatraz Smedry, an orphan whose neglectful grandfather lets him wither away in foster homes for the first 13 years of his life (Dumbledore much?). The Smedry family is infamous for the talents that grace each individual member; Alcatraz has an extraordinary talent for breaking things. Because of this talent foster families are quick to give him up, resulting in Alcatraz bei</span>
  <span id="freeText1375923299696389559" style="display:none">5 stars for pure entertainment value. I laughed my ass off reading this book. <br><br>Alcatraz Versus the Evil Librarians is about Alcatraz Smedry, an orphan whose neglectful grandfather lets him wither away in foster homes for the first 13 years of his life (Dumbledore much?). The Smedry family is infamous for the talents that grace each individual member; Alcatraz has an extraordinary talent for breaking things. Because of this talent foster families are quick to give him up, resulting in Alcatraz being passed around like a bong from home to home, until on his 13th birthday he receives his inheritance in the mail: a bag of sand. <br><br><b>BUT WAIT!</b> If at this point you're thinking you want to skip this book, let me tell you that it includes all of the following:<b><br>- a sarcastic sword-wielding teenage girl<br>- dinosaurs with posh British accents<br>- walking romance novels<br>- lots and lots of fourth wall breaking<br>- shotguns<br>- a spidey sense that involves tripping rather than tingling<br>- cantaloupes and coconuts<br></b>There. That ought to convince you to read the series. <br><br>So Alcatraz's sand gets stolen by his foster care agent who is secretly an evil librarian. Then Grandpa Smedry, whose special talent is being late, arrives 13 years late to Alcatraz's life and fails to save his grandson from the trauma of foster care and being an orphan. Smh.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381188310ra/4480651.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>To make it up to him, Grandpa Smedry takes him on a perilous adventure to recover the bag of sand. <br><br>Alcatraz's narration is absolutely hilarious. Nearly every chapter he stops the story to talk directly to the reader, like so: <blockquote>
<i>If you are anything like me - clever, fond of goat cheese, devilishly handsome - then you have undoubtedly read many books. And, while reading those books, you likely have thought that you are smarter than the characters in those books. <br>You're just imagining things.<br>Now, I've already spoken about foreshadowing (a meddling literary convention of which Heisenberg would uncertainly be proud). However, there are other reasons why you only </i>think<i> that you're smarter than the characters in this book. ...</i>
</blockquote> <b>Extra points to anyone who just got that Physics joke.</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470743958ra/19959457.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As you can see, Alcatraz is a funny guy. If you ask me, this whole series is a way for Brandon Sanderson to let his humorous side show and speak through Alcatraz.<br>In fact, <b>Brandon Sanderson proved all my suspicions about the nature of authors are true</b>: <blockquote>
  <i>Authors write books for one, and only one, reason: because we like to torture people.<br>Now, actual torture is frowned upon in civilized society. Fortunately, the authorial community has discovered in storytelling an even more powerful - and more fulfilling - means of causing agony in others. We write stories. And by doing so, we engage in a perfectly legal method of doing all kinds of mean and terrible things to our readers.</i>
</blockquote> I KNEW IT.<br><br>I'm buddy reading the whole series in preparation of the release of Book 5, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18714787.The_Dark_Talent__Alcatraz___5_" title="The Dark Talent (Alcatraz, #5) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dark Talent</a>, with the wonderful readers over at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">BB&amp;B</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1375923299696389559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
