<div id="review_2789950663" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2789950663" />
    <a title="Celeste" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste"><img alt="Celeste" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481055226p2/7317186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2789950663?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste">Celeste</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25753608-alcatraz-vs-the-evil-librarians">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=childrens-books">childrens-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2789950663" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4442831242726553473"><i>You can find <a href='https://wp.me/pa0WBY-sG' rel='nofollow noopener'>this</a> review and more at <a href='http://novelnotions.net' rel='nofollow noopener'>Novel Notions</a>. </i><br/><br/>Is anyone else hesitant to read a favorite author’s work outside of their usual genre? I’ve loved Brandon Sanderson for years, but I’ve been extremely reluctant to try his young adult or middle grade offerings. I know that he writes addictive, immersive adult fantasy and was afraid to find out if that carried over into other genres intended for radically different audiences. I shouldn’t have doubted him. <b><i>Alcatraz Versus the Evil Librarians</i> was </b></span>
  <span id="freeText4442831242726553473" style="display:none"><i>You can find <a href="https://wp.me/pa0WBY-sG" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> review and more at <a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a>. </i><br /><br />Is anyone else hesitant to read a favorite author’s work outside of their usual genre? I’ve loved Brandon Sanderson for years, but I’ve been extremely reluctant to try his young adult or middle grade offerings. I know that he writes addictive, immersive adult fantasy and was afraid to find out if that carried over into other genres intended for radically different audiences. I shouldn’t have doubted him. <b><i>Alcatraz Versus the Evil Librarians</i> was my first foray into Sanderson’s middle grade books, and it definitely won’t be my last.</b> <br /><blockquote>“If you don't believe what I'm telling you, then ask yourself this: would any decent, kind-hearted individual become a writer? Of course not.”</blockquote><br />First of all, who names their protagonist Alcatraz Smedry? Sanderson, that’s who. The silliness of that name sets the tone for the entire book, in my opinion. His story opens on his 13th birthday when a gift from one or both of his birth parents arrives on the doorstep of his current foster home. It’s sand. Yep, sand. Not exactly the kind of gift you hope to receive from parents you’ve never met and aren’t even sure are still alive. So Alcatraz starts doing what he does best as he processes this unusual gift; he break things. It’s this talent for breaking things that has kept the multitude of foster families who have taken him in over the years from keeping Alcatraz for very long. And who can blame them? Alcatraz sure doesn’t.<br /><blockquote>“Authors also create lovable, friendly characters, then proceed to do terrible things to them, like throw them in unsightly librarian-controlled dungeons. This makes readers feel hurt and worried for the characters. The simple truth is that authors like making people squirm. If this weren't the case, all novels would be filled completely with cute bunnies having birthday parties.”</blockquote><br />The story spirals from there. Alcatraz is visited by Grandpa Smedry, who he has never even met. The bag of sand, which Alcatraz had thought such a pointless gift, is actually super important and has been stolen by Alcatraz’s social worker while he wasn’t paying attention. Come to find out, said social worker is actually part of a cabal of evil librarians who have taken over the majority of the world. And Alcatraz is actually a member of a famous family of Free Kingdomers, those still battling against the librarians in hopes of saving the world. Who would’ve guessed?<br /><blockquote>“By now it is probably very late at night, and you have stayed up to read this book when you should have gone to sleep. If this is the case, then I commend you for falling into my trap. It is a writer’s greatest pleasure to hear that someone was kept up until the unholy hours of the morning reading one of his books.”</blockquote><br />As he begins his search for this weirdly important bag of sand with Grandpa Smedry, Alcatraz learns that basically everything he knows is a lie. The world is not what he thinks it is. There’s a family out there that loves him, and sees him as smart and talented instead of a mess. And librarians are evil. Never forget that librarians are out to get you. Which I found surprising information, seeing as I once worked as a children’s librarian. Thank goodness I managed to escape before I got in too deep.<br /><blockquote>“You see, that is the sad, sorry, terrible thing about sarcasm.<br /><br />It's really funny.” </blockquote><br /><b>My favorite thing about this book is Alcatraz’s voice.</b> He is one of the snarkiest, most sarcastic narrators I’ve ever come across and I absolutely love it. Very rarely is a narrator’s voice as strong and self-aware as the voice Sanderson delivered through Alcatraz, and I was ecstatic to find that in this book. Also, this book is just so funny on multiple levels. The plot and the characters are silly in the best way, which I think will really appeal to readers, especially those in the target audience. But Sanderson also uses Alcatraz to voice some hilarious views on books and reading and authorship, which to me was the best part of the story and is the one of the two reasons I rounded my 4.5 star rating up instead of down.<br /><blockquote>“Authors write books for one, and only one, reason: because we like to torture people.”</blockquote><br />The other reason I rounded up my rating is how <b>the magic system mirrors the foundation of Sanderson’s faith</b>. In this novel, Alcatraz finds out that he is an oculator, one who can use different lenses to see or interact differently with the world. If you think that the idea of glasses helping to hone power feels oddly familiar, you’re not wrong. According to tradition, Joseph Smith, the founder of the Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints, was led by the angel Moroni to a set of golden plates that contained the Book of Mormon. Human eyes were unable to translate the markings, but two stones known as the Urim and Thummim were preserved in the same stone box as the plate. Smith used these stones as lens through which to translate the plates. While this legend has since been questioned by scholars both within and outside of the LDS church, I feel that it’s not a stretch to imagine that Sanderson used this story as a bit of inspiration for the Smedry family’s oculatory powers.<br /><blockquote>“Alcatraz actually knows a person named Brandon Sanderson. That man, however, is a fantasy writer and is therefore prone to useless bouts of delusion in literary form.”</blockquote><br /><b>This book was an absolute joy to read.</b> If I was still a teacher, I would undoubtedly be reading this book to my classes, and pushing it into the hands of other students. I will definitely be reading the next book, and will probably read the rest of the series. Sorry for doubting you, Sanderson. I should’ve known that you can write amazing fantasy for any age, and that readers of any age could enjoy the books you aim at younger readers. I promise not to doubt you again.<br /><br /><i>As I am not a member of the LDS Church, please be aware that I can neither speak for the church nor explain their beliefs. If you’re interested in learning more about Joseph Smith, you can visit the Joseph Smith Foundation <a href="http://ldsanswers.org/joseph-smith-translate-plates-book-mormon-came-forth/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>. To learn more about the LDS Church, you can visit their official website <a href="https://www.lds.org/?lang=eng" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4442831242726553473" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1760777330" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1760777330" />
    <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale"><img alt="Hannah Greendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466436186p2/43377498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1760777330?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah Greendale" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale">Hannah Greendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780439925525" href="/book/show/3537527-alcatraz-versus-the-evil-librarians">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1760777330" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14213281996266736254">When Alcatraz received his inheritance on this thirteenth birthday, he never expected it to be a bag of sand. But then again, his parents named him Alcatraz, so it's no wonder they left him something bizarre. Turns out, it's no ordinary bag of sand, and Alcatraz is no ordinary orphan boy. He's about to embark on an adventure where a cult of evil Librarians rule the world, and the only way he can stop them is to venture into the depths of a labyrinthine library armed with a pair of eyeglasses and</span>
  <span id="freeText14213281996266736254" style="display:none">When Alcatraz received his inheritance on this thirteenth birthday, he never expected it to be a bag of sand. But then again, his parents named him Alcatraz, so it's no wonder they left him something bizarre. Turns out, it's no ordinary bag of sand, and Alcatraz is no ordinary orphan boy. He's about to embark on an adventure where a cult of evil Librarians rule the world, and the only way he can stop them is to venture into the depths of a labyrinthine library armed with a pair of eyeglasses and a knack for breaking most everything he touches. <br /><br />The author brings a wonderful sense of humor to this book: <br /><br /><i>Remember, despite the fact that this book is being sold as a "fantasy" novel, you must take all of the things it says extremely seriously, as they are quite important, are in no way silly, and always make sense. <br />Rutabaga.</i><br /><br />The story is told from the perspective of Alcatraz as a grownup. His tone and syntax are much more adult than a thirteen-year-old boy's, so the book feels a bit stuffy at times. Also, nearly every chapter begins with the narrator pausing the story to address the reader. These sections slow the action and are very repetitive. <br /><br /><i>At this point, perhaps you Hushlanders are beginning to doubt the truth of this narrative. You have seen several odd and inexplicable things happen. (Though, just as a warning, the story so far has actually been quite tame. Just wait until we get to the part with the talking dinosaurs.) Some readers might even think that I'm just making this story up. You might think that everything in this book is dreamy silliness.</i> <br /><br />Another point of contention: While the author had the good intention of writing a fun story for kids, he puts a fair amount of emphasis on guns, something that starts to feel uncomfortable after a while. One of the characters carries a bag full of guns -- shotguns, uzis, pistols. The merits of swords vs. guns are debated. At one point, it's even suggested that if a thirteen-year-old boy were to find an uzi lying on the ground, the natural thing to do would be to pick it up: <br /><br /><i>As she did, I noticed the discarded uzi, lying ignored on the floor. Trying to look nonchalant, I wandered over to it, absently reaching down and picking it up. <br />This is, I would like to note, precisely the same thing</i> any<i> thirteen-year-old boy would do in that situation. A boy who wouldn't do such a thing probably hasn't been reading enough books about killer Librarians.</i><br /><br />Obviously the guns aren't mentioned with the intent of delivering a bad message, but in a book with talking dinosaurs, laser eyeglasses, and monsters made of crumpled paper, it seems like it would have been all-too-easy to swap the guns for something else more imaginative. Why not Super Soakers filled with a stunning potion or with liquid ice that freezes ones opponent? <br /><br />Despite some elements that were personally unappealing, it's safe to assume that middle graders will enjoy <i>Alcatraz Verses the Evil Librarians</i>. It's a fanciful adventure of secret worlds, lost languages, and super cool eye-wear. <br /><br /><br />Random Thought: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Is this passage a slam on Harry Potter? <i>"What did you expect? That I'd leave you here all summer, in the exact place where your enemies know where to look? With people that aren't even your family? In a place you don't really like, and that is depressingly normal compared to the world you've grown to love? Doesn't that sound a little stupid and contrived to you?"</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> </span>
  <a data-text-id="14213281996266736254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

It comes across to me as smug. To illustrate, here are some of the author's own words (strewn throughout the story)...<br><br><b>
  <i>"Are you annoyed with me yet? Good. I've worked very hard. Honestly, authors can be so self-indulgent."</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>"Authors write books for one, and only one, reason. Because we like to torture people."</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>"Now, if you're ever writing a story such as this, you should know something. Never interrupt the flow of a good action scene by interjecting needless explanations."</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497560021ra/23037531.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>While Sanderson obviously has talent, imho it is lost in "Alcatraz Versus the Evil Librarians" due to his most annoying technique of relentlessly telling the reader what to think and how to feel. <b>Maybe</b> this strategy works with 8-year-olds, but I (not an 8-year-old) was so aggravated that I couldn't wait to be done with this book. The <b>ONLY</b> reason I didn't DNF it was because it fulfilled a challenge.<br><br>You may be confused by my rating since 3 stars means "liked it". I truly hated reading this book so you'd think I'd only give it 1 star.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479101574ra/21147048.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>However...</i>

If I could have deleted all the "asides", I would have given it 5 stars. So, I went down the middle. I hope that's considered fair.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765378941" href="/book/show/25403108-alcatraz-vs-the-evil-librarians">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8575414-emma?shelf=childrns">childrns</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8575414-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1693419005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2722901469843741552">If I was a middle grader, this would definitely be a 5 star read! What a funny, surreal and original story! It really is very charming. Evil baddies ( Librarians) and a hilarious cast of heros who have talents that you have never seen before, battle it out in (and I hope this isn't a spoiler!) a library..<br/><br/>Alcatraz the hero of our story talks directly to the reader in a way which is very funny and engaging. As a teacher myself, I also approve entirely of the way in which Sanderson almost tutors th</span>
  <span id="freeText2722901469843741552" style="display:none">If I was a middle grader, this would definitely be a 5 star read! What a funny, surreal and original story! It really is very charming. Evil baddies ( Librarians) and a hilarious cast of heros who have talents that you have never seen before, battle it out in (and I hope this isn't a spoiler!) a library..<br /><br />Alcatraz the hero of our story talks directly to the reader in a way which is very funny and engaging. As a teacher myself, I also approve entirely of the way in which Sanderson almost tutors the reader in the craft of writing an engaging story, teaches a child that writing is about crafting and shaping the perfect story to engage the reader.<br /><br />I think Brandon Sanderson must be a very funny guy in real life.<br /><br />It is fantastic to see such an unlikely and vulnerable character as the main protagonist. We see a child of low self esteem with destructive tendencies find the hero inside himself and his place in the world- and that is a very positive message for children and adults alike.<br /><br />This book will make you laugh and it will make you think. Not sure if I personally would continue with the series but I definitely would if I was a few decades younger!</span>

<div id="review_2369404124" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2369404124" />
    <a title="Tessy Ijachi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65798982-tessy-ijachi"><img alt="Tessy Ijachi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560367121p2/65798982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2369404124?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tessy Ijachi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tessy Ijachi" href="/user/show/65798982-tessy-ijachi">Tessy Ijachi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780439925525" href="/book/show/3537527-alcatraz-versus-the-evil-librarians">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65798982-tessy-ijachi?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65798982-tessy-ijachi?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2369404124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6511509887153318009"><b>
  <i>”In the Hushlands – those Librarian-controlled nations such as the United States, Canada, and England – this book will be published as a work of fantasy. Do not be fooled! This is no work of fiction, nor is my name really Brandon Sanderson. Both are guises to hide the book from Librarian agents.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>You have been warned, this is not really a book by Brandon Sanderson but rather by Alcatraz Smedry. I know right? I almost fell for those librarian tricks, it's a good thing I know the truth.<br/><br/>All joke</span>
  <span id="freeText6511509887153318009" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>”In the Hushlands – those Librarian-controlled nations such as the United States, Canada, and England – this book will be published as a work of fantasy. Do not be fooled! This is no work of fiction, nor is my name really Brandon Sanderson. Both are guises to hide the book from Librarian agents.”</i>
</b><br /><br />You have been warned, this is not really a book by Brandon Sanderson but rather by Alcatraz Smedry. I know right? I almost fell for those librarian tricks, it's a good thing I know the truth.<br /><br />All jokes aside, I quite love this book, despite it's weirdness and satire jokes. It's unique in it's own way, who else would have thought of evil librarians. <br />Brandon Sanderson was able to build a world out of the real world which kind of makes me wonder if everything I know about the world are all lies.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>”Desire does not instantly change the world. Sometimes, stories gloss over this fact, for the world would be a much more pleasant place if you could obtain something simply by wanting it badly enough.”</i>
</b><br /><br />The magic system is very unique, at first it seemed really weird and silly. People having weird talents like arriving late and saying things that don't make sense, but I love how it was explained in depth and put into use.<br /><br />Alcatraz was a great character, Along with grandpa Smedry, Bastille, Quentin and Sing. They were really entertaining and weird. <br />I love the way the book was written. There was a lot of internal Monologue from Alcatraz in a way that made it seem like he really wrote the book.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>”Some people assume that authors write books because we have vivid imaginations and want to share our vision. Other people assume that authors write because we are bursting with stories, and therefore must scribble those stories down in moments of creative propondidty.<br />Both groups of people are completely wrong. Authors write books for one, and only one, reason: because we like to torture people.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Can't wait to read the next book and see what next the evil librarians throw at Alcatraz.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6511509887153318009" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_253933144" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/253933144" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/253933144?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780439925525" href="/book/show/3537527-alcatraz-versus-the-evil-librarians">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=ebook_nook">ebook_nook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=humorous">humorous</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer253933144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14074433640982917742">I'm shelving this as "fantasy" because, well... I don't want to call the attention of the Librarians down upon my head. They're mean and will probably try to kill me for letting the cat out of the bag. This book was banned, and for good reason. Hopefully, they'll just look at the shelf tags, and not the actual review. I don't want to be silenced. <br/><br/>Alcatraz Smedry (writing as some "Brandon Sanderson" guy as a cover) tells his story, and quite a story it is. Librarians have been keeping us all in t</span>
  <span id="freeText14074433640982917742" style="display:none">I'm shelving this as "fantasy" because, well... I don't want to call the attention of the Librarians down upon my head. They're mean and will probably try to kill me for letting the cat out of the bag. This book was banned, and for good reason. Hopefully, they'll just look at the shelf tags, and not the actual review. I don't want to be silenced. <br /><br />Alcatraz Smedry (writing as some "Brandon Sanderson" guy as a cover) tells his story, and quite a story it is. Librarians have been keeping us all in the dark about the real way of the world. Seven continents? Try ten. Dinosaurs extinct? Not hardly. They are quite alive, and very cultured and polite. Magic isn't real? Well, ok, that one's true. But only because the people who can use it call it "technology" not magic. <br /><br />So, I mean, you can kind of see how they'd want their version of "reality" to be the norm. Well it's not the norm. Jeez. Sheep... Don't know anything. <br /><br />Alcatraz tells his story in unique fashion... essentially talking directly to the reader, telling them about the story, about writing the story, about authors, and about himself. He's bluntly honest, and it's quite commendable. Most authors won't tell you that they write out of pure desire to cause their readers distress... but they do. Only Alcatraz is honest enough to say so, because he wants to prove his honesty about the rest of the "unbelievable" things he's sharing. I trust him. You should too. <br /><br />One thing that kind of annoyed me was that there were a lot of typos and misspellings in this story. I'm fairly certain that that's just evil Librarians trying to discredit Alcatraz, but it could have been the conversion to ebook as well. Things like spelling "pterodactyl" as "peteridactyl" and then "pteridactle" before spelling it correctly the 3rd time. Or using "remarkable" when it should be "remarkably". Like I said, I think it was the Librarians. They are remarkable devious. <br /><br />See what they did?? <br /><br />All in all, this is a "fun" adventure "story". I'd definitely recommend it. Read it, and have your eyes opened. They probably need it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14074433640982917742" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_33629312" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33629312" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/446464-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316545868p2/446464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33629312?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/446464-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone looking for a zany and slightly philosophical look at a world ruled by evil Librarians!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446464-kathryn?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi">fantasy-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446464-kathryn?shelf=childrens-picture-books">childrens-picture-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446464-kathryn?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33629312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9154695064255108994">We met Brandon Sanderson at a book reading/signing yesterday. Such fun! He seemed very nice and thoroughly excited about his creations. Younger than I'd expected and also very "normal" but fun. Most people were there for his other (adult fantasy) books and the majority of the Q&A revolved around his taking over the "Wheel of Time" series now that its original author has passed away. I think, for this reason, he was extremely excited when we showed up with a copy of "Alcatraz" for him to sign! :-</span>
  <span id="freeText9154695064255108994" style="display:none">We met Brandon Sanderson at a book reading/signing yesterday. Such fun! He seemed very nice and thoroughly excited about his creations. Younger than I'd expected and also very "normal" but fun. Most people were there for his other (adult fantasy) books and the majority of the Q&amp;A revolved around his taking over the "Wheel of Time" series now that its original author has passed away. I think, for this reason, he was extremely excited when we showed up with a copy of "Alcatraz" for him to sign! :-p I told him I originally found a copy IN THE LIBRARY, which is, of course, a most amazing feat! ;-&gt; We chatted for a few minutes. He said that the idea just sort of came to him after he got the opening sentence in his head. He wrote the book just on a whim, a very personal endeavor, kind of a break from his heavier, lengthier (i.e., 300,000 words!) fantasy novels. He just wrote without really having a preconceived notion of what would happen and he had a great time. He wasn't sure if anyone else would enjoy the zaniness but, tada!, it got published and did find some loyal fans. I told him that my husband and I appreciated the "deeper levels" of the philosophy and political aspects and he seemed to get really excited about that--perhaps he is more used to kids who haven't really studied Thomas Aquinas yet, haha. So, we had a good time and it was so nice to meet him.<br />*************************************************************<br />What a wacky, wise book! I really don't know how to describe it. It's not exactly the sort of book you cozy down with and I'm not sure how attached I really felt to the characters (One chapter begins with Alcatraz asking the reader, "Are you annoyed with me yet?" and he constantly asserts that he is not as heroic or as nice as the Free Kingdomers have made him out to be.)<br /><br />AND YET, I was completely absorbed in it! Despite all the goofy, fantastical sorts of things going on, Sanderson makes some philosophical and political forays (Plato's allegory of the cave is even mentioned!) Consider these quotes, "People go along with what they're told. Even intelligent people believe what they read and hear, assuming they're given no reason to question." <br /><br />I think the best way to give any sort of description of the book is to include a few quotes to give you a sense of the writing style--which could be maddeningly annoying to son:<br /><br />"Hushlanders [that's us], I'd like to take this opportunity to commend you for reading this book. I realize the difficulty you must have gone through to obtain it--after all, no Librarian is likekly to recommend it, considering the secrets it exposes about their kind. <br /><br />Actually, my experience has been that people generally don't recommend this kind of book at all. It is far too interesting. Perhpas you have had other kinds of books recommended to you. Perhaps, even, you have been given books by friends, parents or teachers, then told that these books are the type you 'have to read.' Those books are invariably described as 'important' -- which, in my experience, pretty much means that they're boring. (Words like 'meaningful' and 'thoughtful' are other good clues.)<br /><br />If there is a boy in these kinds of books, he will not go on an adventure to fight against Librarians, paper monsters, and one-eyed Dark Oculators. In fact, the lad will not go on an adventure or fight agaisnt anything at all. Instead, his dog will die. Or, in some cases, his mother will die. If it's a REALLY meaningful book, both his dog AND his mother will die. (Apparently most writers have things against dogs and mothers.)<br /><br />Neither my mother nor my dog dies in this book. I'm rather tired of those types of stories... To combat such silliness, I've written the volume you hold now--a solid, true account. Hopefully it will help anchor you in reality."<br /><br />There are so many little gems of hilarious-wiseness in the book; so many "Ah, well, that is because the Librarians rule the Hushlands and so things are this way." (Consider, for example, why we use PAPER for our big currency; what else would Librarians choose!?) But, finding them is the whole fun of the book so I'll keep quiet! :-&gt;<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9154695064255108994" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It's a middle reader title and I'm not sure how I would have felt about it as a kid but as an adult I don't care much for hokey humor. The narrator is also constantly pausing to make asides to the reader, to point things out or to say things like "ha fooled you" which this adult reader found obnoxious. But you know, how many books have unique magic systems fighting against </span>
  <span id="freeText6428318262405565193" style="display:none">One of the books on my 2009 TBR list, I finally read Alcatraz versus the Evil Librarians as part of my TBR Explode project. It's a middle reader title and I'm not sure how I would have felt about it as a kid but as an adult I don't care much for hokey humor. The narrator is also constantly pausing to make asides to the reader, to point things out or to say things like "ha fooled you" which this adult reader found obnoxious. But you know, how many books have unique magic systems fighting against evil librarians? <br /><br />You can hear more about this book back on <a href="http://readingenvy.blogspot.com/2016/09/reading-envy-069-evil-librarian-sfbrp.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Episode 069 of the Reading Envy Podcast</a>, where Luke and Juliane discuss it after reading it together.</span>

<div id="review_1721759815" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1721759815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer745125117698479387"><b>***Wanda's Summer Carnival of Children's Literature***</b><br/><br/>Cute, funny, and smart. Add in a coterie of Evil Librarians, plus magical skills acquired through the wearing of lenses (i.e. glasses). Also very meta, in that the author talks directly to the reader. A lot.<br/><br/>Of course, working in libraries, I was predisposed to love this. (Although I shouldn’t—I should be suppressing this work, like a good Evil Librarian).<br/><br/>I would recommend it for children who are dismayed about needing glasses. I think it woul</span>
  <span id="freeText745125117698479387" style="display:none"><b>***Wanda's Summer Carnival of Children's Literature***</b><br /><br />Cute, funny, and smart. Add in a coterie of Evil Librarians, plus magical skills acquired through the wearing of lenses (i.e. glasses). Also very meta, in that the author talks directly to the reader. A lot.<br /><br />Of course, working in libraries, I was predisposed to love this. (Although I shouldn’t—I should be suppressing this work, like a good Evil Librarian).<br /><br />I would recommend it for children who are dismayed about needing glasses. I think it would be an encouraging book for them and make their glasses seem more like the useful tools that they actually are.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="745125117698479387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_38951955" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38951955" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1710557-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475336903p2/1710557.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38951955?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/1710557-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1710557-amy?shelf=bookcrossing">bookcrossing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1710557-amy?shelf=home-library">home-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1710557-amy?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1710557-amy?shelf=met-or-know-the-author">met-or-know-the-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1710557-amy?shelf=kids-of-most-ages">kids-of-most-ages</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1710557-amy?shelf=somewhat-disappointing">somewhat-disappointing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38951955" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6770090992631176825">I'm so bummmed....I've been wanting to read this book since I first heard about it about a year ago. I <i>really</i> wanted to like it because:<br/><br/>1. it's got a great title<br/>2. I've met the author and think he's delightful and a nice guy to boot<br/>3. children's literature is due another winner<br/>4. did I mention I really like the title?<br/>5. the bits I'd read seemed good<br/>6. the concept held promise<br/>7. (I don't really have a seventh reason, but the number 6 seemed icky to end on. Seven has such strength and balance that</span>
  <span id="freeText6770090992631176825" style="display:none">I'm so bummmed....I've been wanting to read this book since I first heard about it about a year ago. I <i>really</i> wanted to like it because:<br /><br />1. it's got a great title<br />2. I've met the author and think he's delightful and a nice guy to boot<br />3. children's literature is due another winner<br />4. did I mention I really like the title?<br />5. the bits I'd read seemed good<br />6. the concept held promise<br />7. (I don't really have a seventh reason, but the number 6 seemed icky to end on. Seven has such strength and balance that I much prefer it.)<br /><br />So anyhow, at the beginning, I was smiling when reading. Alcatraz's style of narrative was amusing. The refrain of "I'm not a nice person" a nice twist. But, for me, it quickly wore thin, and I found myself doing a lot of eye-rolling. It's not that Sanderson is a bad writer. The style just wore thin rather quickly. The pace was rather frenetic, almost as if there were all these good, or clever ideas that he wanted to cram into the book and shoved them into the story plot. But still, every time I'd get annoyed, Sanderson would slip in an allusion that would really make me smile, some that only Monty Python fans, or philosophy students might get. Bravo!<br /><br />Having said all that, I didn't dislike the book. I've certainly read many far worse. I was just disappointed. I suppose that if I didn't hold Brandon (who is finishing the Wheel of Time series after the death of Robert Jordan) to such high standards and high hopes, I might have been more satisfied. It also doesn't help that I read the book during what was a contender for "worst day ever" award. (I kid you not: bad news, traffic violation, flat tire, no $$ in wallet at cash register, dead mobile phone, tension headache and run out of gas all within a half hour.) The jury is still out on if I'll read a sequel, though. Ask me again when my headache goes away.<br /><br />PS A friend just reminded me about a part of the book I, too, really liked. She said, " The part that has stuck with me, and that I laughed and laughed about was the part where Alcatraz was talking about the books that were required reading: they always involved the death of a dog, or the death of a mother, or in some the death of both. "</span>
  <a data-text-id="6770090992631176825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12909193-ohwell?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12909193-ohwell?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12909193-ohwell?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2545380859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3593620836739481217">Fast-paced, delightful and full of humour. The story is unexpected and so is the magic system, but I have to say my favourite part is Brandon Sanderson poking fun at being a writer. The musings at the beginning of each chapter are priceless! Here is just one to whet your appetite:<br/><br/><i>It is a writer’s greatest pleasure to hear that someone was kept up until the unholy hours of the morning reading one of his books. It goes back to authors being terrible people who delight in the suffering of others. P</i></span>
  <span id="freeText3593620836739481217" style="display:none">Fast-paced, delightful and full of humour. The story is unexpected and so is the magic system, but I have to say my favourite part is Brandon Sanderson poking fun at being a writer. The musings at the beginning of each chapter are priceless! Here is just one to whet your appetite:<br /><br /><i>It is a writer’s greatest pleasure to hear that someone was kept up until the unholy hours of the morning reading one of his books. It goes back to authors being terrible people who delight in the suffering of others. Plus we get a kickback from the caffeine industry.</i> LOL<br /><br />And a sobering thought:<br /><i>Even intelligent people believe what they read and hear, assuming they’re given no reason to question.</i><br /><br />Go ahead and read the book! If you can get the audio version, that's even better.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QvagiHif5REWWAyKvIvHH9Rt0GIjX+O3omssD55RthW7n6i3qekFuWrufpe1t/vDTQnrla7nUAW1Pc4rqxV+tg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CFhEr0ExmIXWcPZUgr2CCSyyfy3MjOmCo90zKI4Ib5fxMUyQkEd4LarGhEmLgb7VtdZE2kE0WjC0i9EMu0ynNA==')})
  }

Bruce McComiskey analyzes the instances of bullshit, fake news, feigned ethos, <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText2322229148642262647\" style=\"display:none\">Post-Truth Rhetoric and Composition is a timely exploration of the increasingly widespread and disturbing effect of “post-truth” on public discourse in the United States. Bruce McComiskey analyzes the instances of bullshit, fake news, feigned ethos, hyperbole, and other forms of post-truth rhetoric employed in recent political discourse.\n\nThe book frames “post-truth” within rhetorical theory, referring to the classic triad of logos, ethos, and pathos. McComiskey shows that it is the loss of grounding in logos that exposes us to the dangers of post-truth. As logos is the realm of fact, logic, truth, and valid reasoning, Western society faces increased risks—including violence, unchecked libel, and tainted elections—when the value of reason is diminished and audiences allow themselves to be swayed by pathos and ethos. Evaluations of truth are deferred or avoided, and mendacity convincingly masquerades as a valid form of argument.\n\nIn a post-truth world, where neither truth nor falsehood has reliable meaning, language becomes purely strategic, without reference to anything other than itself. This scenario has serious consequences not only for our public discourse but also for the study of composition.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"2322229148642262647\" href=\"#\"       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson">About Brandon Sanderson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1394044556p3/38550.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson">Brandon Sanderson
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
154,117
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4450684901409533745">Brandon’s major books for the second half of 2016 are <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18714787.The_Dark_Talent' title='The Dark Talent' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dark Talent</a>,</i> the final volume in Alcatraz Smedry’s autobiographical account of his battle against the Evil Librarians who secretly rule our world, and <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28595941.Arcanum_Unbounded' title='Arcanum Unbounded' rel='nofollow noopener'>Arcanum Unbounded</a>,</i> the collection of short fiction in the Cosmere universe that includes the Mistborn series and the Stormlight <br/>Archive, among others. This collection features <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578175.The_Emperor_s_Soul' title='The Emperor’s Soul' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Emperor’s S</a></i></span>
  <span id="freeText4450684901409533745" style="display:none">Brandon’s major books for the second half of 2016 are <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18714787.The_Dark_Talent" title="The Dark Talent" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dark Talent</a>,</i> the final volume in Alcatraz Smedry’s autobiographical account of his battle against the Evil Librarians who secretly rule our world, and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28595941.Arcanum_Unbounded" title="Arcanum Unbounded" rel="nofollow noopener">Arcanum Unbounded</a>,</i> the collection of short fiction in the Cosmere universe that includes the Mistborn series and the Stormlight <br />Archive, among others. This collection features <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578175.The_Emperor_s_Soul" title="The Emperor’s Soul" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emperor’s Soul</a>,</i> <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28698036.Mistborn__Secret_History" title="Mistborn: Secret History" rel="nofollow noopener">Mistborn: Secret History</a>,</i> and a brand-new Stormlight Archive novella, <i>Edgedancer</i>.<br /><br />Earlier this year he released <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15704486.Calamity" title="Calamity" rel="nofollow noopener">Calamity</a>,</i> the finale of the #1 New York Times bestselling Reckoners trilogy that began with <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17182126.Steelheart" title="Steelheart" rel="nofollow noopener">Steelheart</a>
</i>.<br /><br />Brandon Sanderson was born in 1975 in Lincoln, Nebraska. As a child Brandon enjoyed reading, but he lost interest in the types of titles often suggested to him, and by junior high he never cracked a book if he could help it. This changed when an eighth grade teacher gave him <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/176268.Dragonsbane" title="Dragonsbane" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonsbane</a>
</i> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10333.Barbara_Hambly" title="Barbara Hambly" rel="nofollow noopener">Barbara Hambly</a>.<br /><br />Brandon was working on his thirteenth novel when Moshe Feder at Tor Books bought the sixth he had written. Tor has published <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68427.Elantris" title="Elantris" rel="nofollow noopener">Elantris</a>,</i> the Mistborn trilogy and its followup <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10803121.The_Alloy_of_Law" title="The Alloy of Law" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alloy of Law</a>,</i> <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1268479.Warbreaker" title="Warbreaker" rel="nofollow noopener">Warbreaker</a>,</i> and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7235533.The_Way_of_Kings" title="The Way of Kings" rel="nofollow noopener">The Way of Kings</a>
</i> and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11543195.Words_of_Radiance" title="Words of Radiance" rel="nofollow noopener">Words of Radiance</a>,</i> the first two in the planned ten-volume series The Stormlight Archive. He was chosen to complete <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6252.Robert_Jordan" title="Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Jordan</a>’s Wheel of Time series; 2009’s <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1166599.The_Gathering_Storm" title="The Gathering Storm" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gathering Storm</a>
</i> and 2010’s <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8253920.Towers_of_Midnight" title="Towers of Midnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Towers of Midnight</a>
</i> were followed by the final book in the series, <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1166599.A_Memory_of_Light" title="A Memory of Light" rel="nofollow noopener">A Memory of Light</a>,</i> in January 2013. Four books in his middle-grade <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/623976.Alcatraz_vs__the_Evil_Librarians" title="Alcatraz vs. the Evil Librarians" rel="nofollow noopener">Alcatraz vs. the Evil Librarians</a>
</i> series have been released in new editions by Starscape, and his novella <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12796771.Infinity_Blade_Awakening" title="Infinity Blade Awakening" rel="nofollow noopener">Infinity Blade Awakening</a>
</i> was an ebook bestseller for Epic Games accompanying their acclaimed <i>Infinity Blade</i> iOS video game series. Two more novellas, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13452375.Legion" title="Legion" rel="nofollow noopener">Legion</a>
</i> and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578175.The_Emperor_s_Soul" title="The Emperor’s Soul" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emperor’s Soul</a>,</i> were released by Subterranean Press and Tachyon Publications in 2012, and 2013 brought two young adult novels, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10137823.The_Rithmatist" title="The Rithmatist" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rithmatist</a>
</i> from Tor and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17182126.Steelheart" title="Steelheart" rel="nofollow noopener">Steelheart</a>
</i> from Delacorte.<br /><br />The only author to make the short list for the David Gemmell Legend Award six times in four years, Brandon won that award in 2011 for <i>The Way of Kings</i>. <i>The Emperor’s Soul</i> won the 2013 Hugo Award for Best Novella. He has appeared on the <i>New York Times</i> Best-Seller List multiple times, with five novels hitting the #1 spot.<br /><br />Currently living in Utah with his wife and children, Brandon teaches creative writing at Brigham Young University.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4450684901409533745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
